   </div>
   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    List of
    <i>
     Nepenthes
    </i>
    species
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>
    <div id="contentSub">
    </div>
    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
     Jump to:
     <a href="#mw-head">
      navigation
     </a>
     ,
     <a href="#p-search">
      search
     </a>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:N._jamban_and_N._lingulata.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="512" data-file-width="384" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/N._jamban_and_N._lingulata.jpg/220px-N._jamban_and_N._lingulata.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/N._jamban_and_N._lingulata.jpg/330px-N._jamban_and_N._lingulata.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7a/N._jamban_and_N._lingulata.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:N._jamban_and_N._lingulata.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Sympatric upper pitchers of
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Nepenthes_jamban" title="Nepenthes jamban">
          N.jamban
         </a>
        </i>
        (left) and
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Nepenthes_lingulata" title="Nepenthes lingulata">
          N.lingulata
         </a>
        </i>
        (right) in Sumatran upper
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Montane_forest" title="Montane forest">
         montane forest
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      This
      <b>
       list of
       <i>
        Nepenthes
       </i>
       species
      </b>
      is a comprehensive listing of all known species of the
      <a href="/wiki/Carnivorous_plant" title="Carnivorous plant">
       carnivorous plant
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Genus" title="Genus">
       genus
      </a>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Nepenthes" title="Nepenthes">
        Nepenthes
       </a>
      </i>
      . It includes 161 recognised
      <a href="/wiki/Extant_taxon" title="Extant taxon">
       extant
      </a>
      species, 3
      <a href="/wiki/Undescribed_taxon" title="Undescribed taxon">
       incompletely diagnosed taxa
      </a>
      , and 3
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nothospecies" title="Nothospecies">
       nothospecies
      </a>
      . Three possible
      <a href="/wiki/Extinction" title="Extinction">
       extinct
      </a>
      species are also covered.
     </p>
     <p>
      The official
      <a href="/wiki/International_Union_for_Conservation_of_Nature" title="International Union for Conservation of Nature">
       IUCN
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Conservation_status" title="Conservation status">
       conservation status
      </a>
      of each species is taken from the latest edition of the
      <a href="/wiki/IUCN_Red_List" title="IUCN Red List">
       IUCN Red List
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-1">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Unofficial assessments based on the IUCN criteria are also included, but are presented in italics. Unless otherwise noted, taxonomic determinations and all other information are sourced from
      <a href="/wiki/Stewart_McPherson_(geographer)" title="Stewart McPherson (geographer)">
       Stewart McPherson
      </a>
      's two-volume
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Pitcher_Plants_of_the_Old_World" title="Pitcher Plants of the Old World">
        Pitcher Plants of the Old World
       </a>
      </i>
      , published in 2009.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McPherson_2-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-McPherson-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Where recent literature provides an altitudinal distribution that falls outside the range given in
      <i>
       Pitcher Plants of the Old World
      </i>
      , the discrepancy is noted.
     </p>
     <p>
      All major islands within a species's geographic range are included. Smaller surrounding islands are listed separately under "Minor islands", though these lists are not exhaustive. In the case of
      <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">
       archipelagos
      </a>
      such as the
      <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">
       Philippines
      </a>
      , the individual islands to which the species is native are shown in brackets.
     </p>
     <p>
      Authorities are presented in the form of a standard
      <a href="/wiki/Author_citation_(botany)" title="Author citation (botany)">
       author citation
      </a>
      , using abbreviations specified by the
      <a href="/wiki/International_Plant_Names_Index" title="International Plant Names Index">
       International Plant Names Index
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Years given denote the year of the species's formal publication under the current name, thus excluding the earlier
      <a href="/wiki/Basionym" title="Basionym">
       basionym
      </a>
      date of publication if one exists.
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Incompletely_diagnosed_taxa">
       Incompletely diagnosed taxa
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nepenthes_species&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Incompletely diagnosed taxa">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The following
      <a href="/wiki/Undescribed_taxon" title="Undescribed taxon">
       undescribed taxa
      </a>
      are taken from
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Pitcher_Plants_of_the_Old_World" title="Pitcher Plants of the Old World">
        Pitcher Plants of the Old World
       </a>
      </i>
      and its supplementary volume,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/New_Nepenthes" title="New Nepenthes">
        New Nepenthes
       </a>
      </i>
      , published in 2011.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NewMcPherson_55-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-NewMcPherson-55">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        46

         ]

       </a>

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Nothospecies">
       Nothospecies
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nepenthes_species&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Nothospecies">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Jebb" title="Matthew Jebb">
       Matthew Jebb
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Martin_Cheek" title="Martin Cheek">
       Martin Cheek
      </a>
      recognised the following three
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nothospecies" title="Nothospecies">
       nothospecies
      </a>
      in their monographs on the genus ("
      <a href="/wiki/A_skeletal_revision_of_Nepenthes_(Nepenthaceae)" title="A skeletal revision of Nepenthes (Nepenthaceae)">
       A skeletal revision of
       <i>
        Nepenthes
       </i>
       (Nepenthaceae)
      </a>
      " (1997) and "
      <a href="/wiki/Nepenthaceae_(2001_monograph)" title="Nepenthaceae (2001 monograph)">
       Nepenthaceae
      </a>
      " (2001)). In the recent literature, these taxa have generally been treated as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Natural_hybrid" title="Natural hybrid">
       natural hybrids
      </a>
      rather than as species.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McPherson_2-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-McPherson-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clarke2001_18-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-Clarke2001-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-C.26J_25-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-C.26J-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clarke1997_26-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Clarke1997-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Of the three,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Nepenthes_%C3%97_kinabaluensis" title="Nepenthes  kinabaluensis">
        N.kinabaluensis
       </a>
      </i>
      has the strongest claim to species status, as it grows in two large, self-sustaining populations independent of its putative parent species.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-C.26J_25-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-C.26J-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
       <a href="#cite_note-103">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      These populations are reportedly true breeding.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-C.26J_25-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-C.26J-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Jumaat_Haji_Adam" title="Jumaat Haji Adam">
       Jumaat Haji Adam
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/C._C._Wilcock" title="C. C. Wilcock">
       C. C. Wilcock
      </a>
      advocated the recognition of
      <i>
       N.kinabaluensis
      </i>
      as a species in a 1998 article.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
       <a href="#cite_note-104">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <table class="sortable wikitable" width="100%">

       </td>
       <td>
        <a href="/wiki/Borneo" title="Borneo">

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Extinct_species">
       Extinct species
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Nepenthes_species&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Extinct species">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Fossil" title="Fossil">
       Fossil
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Pollen" title="Pollen">
       pollen
      </a>
      of various provenance, much of it originally described under the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Form_taxon_(botany)" title="Form taxon (botany)">
       form taxon
      </a>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Droseridites" title="Droseridites">
        Droseridites
       </a>
      </i>
      , has been tentatively assigned to
      <i>
       Nepenthes
      </i>
      by several authors.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Krutzsch1985_105-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Krutzsch1985-105">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Krutzsch1989_106-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Krutzsch1989-106">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        86
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
       <a href="#cite_note-107">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        87
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The following three species were transferred to the genus
      <i>
       Nepenthes
      </i>
      by Wilfried Krutzsch in 1985.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Krutzsch1985_105-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Krutzsch1985-105">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <table class="sortable wikitable" width="100%">
      <tr>
       <th>
        Species
       </th>
       <th>
        Authority
       </th>
       <th>

        Age
       </th>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td>
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Droseridites" title="Droseridites">
          Nepenthes echinatus
         </a>
        </i>
       </td>
       <td>
        (Hunger)
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Wilfried_Krutzsch&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Wilfried Krutzsch (page does not exist)">
         Krutzsch
        </a>
       </td>
       <td>
        1985
       </td>
       <td>
        <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">
         Europe
        </a>
       </td>
       <td>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palaeocene" title="Palaeocene">
         Palaeocene
        </a>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td>
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Droseridites" title="Droseridites">
          Nepenthes echinosporus
         </a>
        </i>
       </td>
       <td>
        (
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Robert_Henri_Hermann_Ernst_Potoni%C3%A9&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Robert Henri Hermann Ernst Potoni (page does not exist)">
         R.Potoni
        </a>
        )
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Wilfried_Krutzsch&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Wilfried Krutzsch (page does not exist)">
         Krutzsch
        </a>
       </td>
       <td>
        1985
       </td>
       <td>
        <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">
         Europe
        </a>
       </td>
       <td>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palaeocene" title="Palaeocene">
         Palaeocene
        </a>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td>
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Droseridites" title="Droseridites">
          Nepenthes major
         </a>
        </i>
       </td>
       <td>
        (
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Wilfried_Krutzsch&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Wilfried Krutzsch (page does not exist)">
         Krutzsch
        </a>
        )
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Wilfried_Krutzsch&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Wilfried Krutzsch (page does not exist)">
         Krutzsch
        </a>
       </td>
       <td>
        1985
       </td>
       <td>
        <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">
         Europe
        </a>
       </td>
       <td>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palaeocene" title="Palaeocene">
         Palaeocene
        </a>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      Some authors consider
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Droseridites_major" title="Droseridites major">
        Droseridites major
       </a>
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Droseridites_parvus" title="Droseridites parvus">
        D.parvus
       </a>
      </i>
      as synonyms of
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nepenthidites_laitryngewensis" title="Nepenthidites laitryngewensis">
        Nepenthidites laitryngewensis
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
       <a href="#cite_note-108">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        88
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
       <a href="#cite_note-109">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Pollen from the
      <a href="/wiki/Kerguelen_Islands" title="Kerguelen Islands">
       Kerguelen Islands
      </a>
      originally described as
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Droseridites_spinosus" title="Droseridites spinosus">
        D.spinosus
       </a>
      </i>
      has also been interpreted as belonging to
      <i>
       Nepenthes
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Meimberg_110-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Meimberg-110">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

      <span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">

      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>

       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="reflist columns references-column-count references-column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2; list-style-type: decimal;">
      <ol class="references">
       <li id="cite_note-alata-7">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         ^
         <a href="#cite_ref-alata_7-0">
          <sup>
           <i>
            <b>
             a
            </b>
           </i>
          </sup>
         </a>
         <a href="#cite_ref-alata_7-1">
          <sup>
           <i>
            <b>
             b
            </b>
           </i>
          </sup>
         </a>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Under the narrow
         <a href="/wiki/Circumscription_(taxonomy)" title="Circumscription (taxonomy)">
          circumscription
         </a>
         of
         <a href="/wiki/Martin_Cheek" title="Martin Cheek">
          Cheek
         </a>
         &amp;
         <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Jebb" title="Matthew Jebb">
          Jebb
         </a>
         (2013),
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Nepenthes_alata" title="Nepenthes alata">
           N.alata
          </a>
         </i>
         is restricted to northern
         <a href="/wiki/Luzon" title="Luzon">
          Luzon
         </a>
         , with the more southerly plants previously referred to this species actually representing
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Nepenthes_graciliflora" title="Nepenthes graciliflora">
           N.graciliflora
          </a>
         </i>
         ,
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Nepenthes_negros" title="Nepenthes negros">
           N.negros
          </a>
         </i>
         , and
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Nepenthes_ramos" title="Nepenthes ramos">
           N.ramos
          </a>
         </i>
         .

           </span>

          </a>

            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-63">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-63">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         The lower altitudinal limit of 2000m given for
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Nepenthes_macrophylla" title="Nepenthes macrophylla">
           N.macrophylla
          </a>
         </i>
         in some older sources
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-J.26C_61-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-J.26C-61">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           51
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
         is apparently incorrect.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McPherson_2-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-McPherson-2">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           2
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
          <a href="#cite_note-62">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           52
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-64">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-64">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Adam, Wilcock &amp; Swaine (1992) give a lower altitudinal limit of 250m for
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Nepenthes_macrovulgaris" title="Nepenthes macrovulgaris">
           N.macrovulgaris
          </a>
         </i>
         .
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AWS1992_8-8">
          <a href="#cite_note-AWS1992-8">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           7
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-76">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-76">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Adam, Wilcock &amp; Swaine (1992) give an upper altitudinal limit of 1500m for
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Nepenthes_rafflesiana" title="Nepenthes rafflesiana">
           N.rafflesiana
          </a>
         </i>
         .
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AWS1992_8-9">
          <a href="#cite_note-AWS1992-8">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           7
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-83">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-83">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Rybka, Rybkov &amp;
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rob_Cantley" title="Rob Cantley">
          Cantley
         </a>
         (2005) give a range of 12001800m for
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Nepenthes_sibuyanensis" title="Nepenthes sibuyanensis">
           N.sibuyanensis
          </a>
         </i>
         ,
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
          <a href="#cite_note-81">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           68
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
         while the authors of the describing paper give a range of 15001800m.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
          <a href="#cite_note-82">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           69
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-86">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-86">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Mansur &amp; Brearley (2008) report finding
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Nepenthes_stenophylla" title="Nepenthes stenophylla">
           N.stenophylla
          </a>
         </i>
         at 400m.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M.26B2008_50-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-M.26B2008-50">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           42
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-90">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-90">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Nepenthes_surigaoensis" title="Nepenthes surigaoensis">
           Nepenthes surigaoensis
          </a>
         </i>
         may grow as high as 1750m ("5750 feet" in the original) according to the describing author,
         <a href="/wiki/Adolph_Daniel_Edward_Elmer" title="Adolph Daniel Edward Elmer">
          Adolph Daniel Edward Elmer
         </a>
         .
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
          <a href="#cite_note-89">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           74
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-93">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-93">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Cheek &amp; Jebb (2001) give an upper altitudinal limit of 2750m for
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Nepenthes_tobaica" title="Nepenthes tobaica">
           N.tobaica
          </a>
         </i>
         .
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-C.26J_25-5">
          <a href="#cite_note-C.26J-25">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           22
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-94">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-94">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Cheek &amp; Jebb (2001) give an upper altitudinal limit of 500m for
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Nepenthes_treubiana" title="Nepenthes treubiana">
           N.treubiana
          </a>
         </i>
         .
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-C.26J_25-6">
          <a href="#cite_note-C.26J-25">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           22
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-96">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-96">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         The upper altitudinal limit of 400m is uncertain as it is based on the figure given on
         <a href="/wiki/Google_Earth" title="Google Earth">
          Google Earth
         </a>
         for an "inexact grid-reference" associated with a herbarium specimen.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ultra_95-5">
          <a href="#cite_note-ultra-95">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           77
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-98">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-98">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Nepenthes_villosa" title="Nepenthes villosa">
           Nepenthes villosa
          </a>
         </i>
         generally grows at elevations of 23003240m, but is more common at 16001900m on
         <a href="/wiki/Mount_Tambuyukon" title="Mount Tambuyukon">
          Mount Tambuyukon
         </a>
         .
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McPherson_2-2">
          <a href="#cite_note-McPherson-2">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           2
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
         Adam, Wilcock &amp; Swaine (1992) give an upper altitudinal limit of 3400m for this species.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AWS1992_8-10">
          <a href="#cite_note-AWS1992-8">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           7
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </span>
       </li>
      </ol>
